data-href="https://ajc.com/news/kemp-says-georgians-have-stepped-up-to-the-plate-to-fight-coronavirus/5QO3NOGMMZD3VGHIKZOLKSUMMU/" data-width="100%" data-numposts="100"></div></div></div><div class="sticky-padding "></div></header></div><main class="c-articleContent"><header class="b-margin-bottom-d30-m20"><div class="c-header"><div class="article-headline-component b-margin-bottom-d30-m20 with-image"><div class="headline"><div class="headline-body"><h1 class="headline-text headline-text-long">Kemp says \xe2\x80\x98Georgians have stepped up to the plate\xe2\x80\x99 to fight coronavirus</h1></div></div><div class="c-image-component "><div class="image-component-image "><div class="lazyload-wrapper"><img src="/pf/resources/logos/AJC/placeholder.svg?d=107" style="width:100%"/></div><div class="c-caption " id="captionID-37183332" on="tap:captionID-37183332.toggleClass(class=&#x27;is-active&#x27;)" role="button" tabindex="0"><div class="photo-caption-btn"><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div><div class="fill-line"></div><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div><div class="fill-line"></div><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div></div><div class="photo-caption"><div class="photo-caption-text">Gov. Brian Kemp wears a &#x27;2020 Census&#x27; branded face mask after encouraging Georgians to fill out the 2020 Census during a press conference at the Georgia State Capitol building in downtown Atlanta, Thursday, Sept. 24, 2020.  (Alyssa Pointer / Alyssa.Pointer@ajc.com)</div><p class="photo-credit-text">Credit: Alyssa Pointer / Alyssa.Pointer@ajc.com</p></div></div></div><p class="photo-credit-text">Credit: Alyssa Pointer / Alyssa.Pointer@ajc.com</p></div></div></div><div style="display:flex;justify-content:center;flex-wrap:wrap" class="c-label-wrapper b-pageContainer b-margin-bottom-d15-m10"><a class="section-label section-label-link" href="/news">News</a><span class="article-timestamp"> | Updated Oct 7, 2020</span></div><div class="b-flexRow b-flexCenter b-pageContainer"><div class="byline b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"><span>By <a href="/staff/j-scott-trubey/">J. Scott Trubey</a> - The Atlanta Journal-Constitution</span><span><a href="/staff/alexis-stevens/">Alexis Stevens</a> - The Atlanta Journal-Constitution</span></div></div><div class="b-flexRow b-flexCenter b-margin-bottom-d15-m10 b-pageContainer"><div class="subheadline-content"><span>But health officials fear possible \xe2\x80\x98twin-demic\xe2\x80\x99 with flu season approaching.</span></div></div></header><article><div class="c-hp01-mp01"></div><div class="c-articleBodyContainer"><div class="free-story-messaging connext-free-messaging b-margin-bottom-d30-m20"></div><div class="c-section\n          full-width b-clear-both\n          b-margin-bottom-d40-m20\n          "><div class="c-contentElements"><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Many Georgians have done their part to help fight the coronavirus, Gov. Brian Kemp said Wednesday.</p></div></div><div class="c-section\n          \n          b-margin-bottom-d40-m20\n          "><div class="c-contentElements"><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">But with the flu season approaching, it\xe2\x80\x99s not the time to back off safety measures to help fight the virus, the governor said at a COVID-19 media briefing.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">\xe2\x80\x9cGeorgians have stepped up to the plate,\xe2\x80\x9d Kemp said. \xe2\x80\x9cThe key is for us to keep doing this. We cannot take our foot off the gas.\xe2\x80\x9d</p></div></div><div class="story-nativo_placeholder--moap b-clear-both"></div><div class="c-section\n          \n          b-margin-bottom-d40-m20\n          "><div class="c-contentElements"><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">[<a href="https://www.ajc.com/news/coronavirus/">Complete coverage of the coronavirus in Georgia</a>]</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Since mid-July, Georgia has reported declining cases in 10 out of the past 11 weeks, an Atlanta Journal-Constitution analysis of state data shows.</p></div></div><div class="c-section"><div class="story-interscroller__placeholder full-width c-clear-both c-contentElements"></div></div><div class="c-section\n          \n          b-margin-bottom-d40-m20\n          "><div class="c-contentElements"><p class="story-subscription__placeholder subscription-promo b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"></p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">The current seven-day rolling average of new cases of 1,159 is down about 70% from the July peak, an AJC analysis of state data found. Hospitalizations also are down from the peak by about 60%.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">But while Georgia has improved in both metrics since the peak, Georgia\xe2\x80\x99s seven-day rolling average of new cases remains about double what it was at the low point at the end of May, a month after Kemp relaxed shelter-in-place orders. The rolling average of people currently hospitalized is about 60% higher than<b> </b>the bottom in early June.</p><div class="c-image-component b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"><div class="image-component-image "><div class="lazyload-wrapper"><img src="/pf/resources/logos/AJC/placeholder.svg?d=107" style="width:100%"/></div><div class="c-caption " id="captionID-10885243" on="tap:captionID-10885243.toggleClass(class=&#x27;is-active&#x27;)" role="button" tabindex="0"><div class="photo-caption-btn"><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div><div class="fill-line"></div><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div><div class="fill-line"></div><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div></div><div class="photo-caption"><div class="photo-caption-text">Journalists sit outside the White House press room during a coronavirus outbreak, Wednesday, Oct. 7, 2020, in Washington. (AP Photo/Evan Vucci)</div><p class="photo-credit-text">Credit: Evan Vucci</p></div></div></div><p class="photo-credit-text">Credit: Evan Vucci</p></div><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">The rate of new coronavirus deaths reported during the seven days that ended Friday also remains higher than the national average, according to the White House Coronavirus Task Force\xe2\x80\x99s latest report from Sunday.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Dr. Harry J. Heiman, a clinical associate professor at the Georgia State University School of Public Health, said Georgia appears to have settled into an elevated plateau in cases that\xe2\x80\x99s double the lows Georgia saw at the end of May.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99ve plateaued at a much higher level than what is desirable,\xe2\x80\x9d Heiman said in an interview earlier this week.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Health officials are concerned about the ongoing pandemic combined with the approaching flu season, according to Dr. Kathleen Toomey, commissioner of the state Department of Public Health.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">COVID-19 and influenza feature similar symptoms, though COVID-19 is more dangerous and more contagious, health experts say.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">\xe2\x80\x9cNever has it been more important to get a flu shot,\xe2\x80\x9d Dr. Toomey<b> </b>said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re trying to prevent twin-demics of COVID plus influenza.\xe2\x80\x9d</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"><b>Georgia in the orange zone</b></p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">President Donald Trump\xe2\x80\x99s coronavirus task force reported on Sunday that Georgia remains in the orange zone for new cases for the second consecutive week.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Orange is the second-most severe zone for new cases in the task force\xe2\x80\x99s four-color coded ranges. Georgia remains in the third, or the yellow zone, for test positivity.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">But both are improvements from the summer.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Most of the major metro areas including Atlanta and Columbus are in the yellow zone for new cases. Savannah and Augusta are in the orange zone, while Rome, Tifton and Toccoa are among eight small metro areas in the red zone.</p><div class="c-image-component b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"><div class="image-component-image "><div class="lazyload-wrapper"><img src="/pf/resources/logos/AJC/placeholder.svg?d=107" style="width:100%"/></div><div class="c-caption " id="captionID-6176252" on="tap:captionID-6176252.toggleClass(class=&#x27;is-active&#x27;)" role="button" tabindex="0"><div class="photo-caption-btn"><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div><div class="fill-line"></div><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div><div class="fill-line"></div><div class="fill-line fill-line-long"></div></div><div class="photo-caption"><div class="photo-caption-text">FILE - In this Aug. 20, 2020, file photo, a student, wearing a face mask, enters the school book store at the University of Georgia in Athens, Ga. The number of Americans newly diagnosed with the coronavirus is falling \xe2\x80\x94 a development experts credit at least partly to increased wearing of masks \xe2\x80\x94 even as the outbreak continues to claim nearly 1,000 lives in the U.S. each day. (Joshua L. Jones/Athens Banner-Herald via AP)</div><p class="photo-credit-text">Credit: Joshua L. Jones</p></div></div></div><p class="photo-credit-text">Credit: Joshua L. Jones</p></div><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Georgia reported a rate of new cases of 77 per 100,000 people for the seven days that ended on Friday, compared to 90 per 100,000 people nationwide. Georgia ranked 28th in new cases after previously ranking as high as worst in the nation in August.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">\xe2\x80\x9cGeorgia has made progress<b>," </b>the White House Coronavirus Task Force report said. "Mitigation efforts must continue to include mask wearing, physical distancing, hand hygiene, and avoiding crowds.\xe2\x80\x9d</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">At his press conference, Kemp sought to highlight improvements at nursing homes and other long-term care facilities, where residents are most vulnerable to the virus.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">On Sept. 15, 172 nursing homes in Georgia were in red zone counties, Kemp said. As of Wednesday morning, that number had declined to 49 facilities.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">The number of nursing homes in green zone counties meanwhile has increased to 69 in that time, up from 19, the governor said.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">An AJC analysis of Department of Community Health data on long-term care homes shows that new coronavirus cases inside facilities have been trending down since July and August.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Kemp also said his administration recently announced $78 million in new reimbursement funds for long-term care centers to boost testing.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">\xe2\x80\x9cIf we all commit to doing the right thing, I am confident we will continue moving in the right direction in the fight against COVID 19,\xe2\x80\x9d Kemp said.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">The latest White House report continues to focus on increasing testing, tackling outbreaks in college towns and reducing spread within long-term care facilities, which can be particularly deadly.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">Georgia reported 129,026 tests in the week ended on Saturday, down 6% compared to the week earlier and down about 36% from the weekly peak in July. But test positivity also hit its lowest weekly rate (7.4%) since June. By Wednesday, the<b> </b>rolling average<b> </b>positivity rate was down to 6%.</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20">\xe2\x80\x9cAre we in a better place than we were two months ago? Absolutely, but we are still not where we need to be,\xe2\x80\x9d Heiman said. \xe2\x80\x9cWe are at risk for significant problems in the coming months based on what\xe2\x80\x99s going on seasonally and weather-wise and with flu season and with schools and in-person instruction.\xe2\x80\x9d</p><p class="story-text b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"><i>AJC data reporter John Perry contributed to this article.</i></p><p class="c-connext hyperlocal_promo b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"></p><p class="c-connext eos-msg__nolog-or-nosub b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"></p></div></div><div class="c-section full-width b-clear-both"><div class="c-relatedList b-margin-bottom-d40-m20"><h1 class="title">In Other News</h1><div class="c-homeListContainer two-columns left-photo-display-class"></div></div></div><div
